Instead, DeltaDiscoveryResponses are a\n   114→// diff to the state of a xDS client.\n   115→// In Delta XDS there are per-resource versions, which allow tracking state at\n   116→// the resource granularity.\n   117→// An xDS Delta session is always in the context of a gRPC bidirectional\n   118→// stream. This allows the xDS server to keep track of the state of xDS clients\n   119→// connected to it.\n   120→//\n   121→// In Delta xDS the nonce field is required and used to pair\n   122→// DeltaDiscoveryResponse to a DeltaDiscoveryRequest ACK or NACK.\n   123→// Optionally, a response message level system_version_info is present for\n   124→// debugging purposes only.\n   125→//\n   126→// DeltaDiscoveryRequest plays two independent roles. Any DeltaDiscoveryRequest\n   127→// can be either or both of: [1] informing the server of what resources the\n   128→// client has gained/lost interest in (using resource_names_subscribe and\n   129→// resource_names_unsubscribe), or [2] (N)ACKing an earlier resource update from\n   130→// the server (using response_nonce, with presence of error_detail making it a NACK).\n   131→// Additionally, the first message (for a given type_url) of a reconnected gRPC stream\n   132→// has a third role: informing the server of the resources (and their versions)\n   133→// that the client already possesses, using the initial_resource_versions field.\n   134→//\n   135→// As with state-of-the-world, when multiple resource types are multiplexed (ADS),\n   136→// all requests/acknowledgments/updates are logically walled off by type_url:\n   137→// a Cluster ACK exists in a completely separate world from a prior Route NACK.\n   138→// In particular, It is only intended for consumption during manual\n  // debugging, the string provided is not guaranteed to be stable across Envoy versions.\n  google.rpc.Status error_detail = 6;\n}\n\n// [#next-free-field: 7]\nmessage DiscoveryResponse {\n  // The version of the response data.\n  string version_info = 1;\n\n  // The response resources. These resources are typed and depend on the API being called.\n  repeated google.protobuf.Any resources = 2;\n\n  // [#not-implemented-hide:]\n  // Canary is used to support two Envoy command line flags:\n  //\n  // * --terminate-on-canary-transition-failure. When set, Envoy is able to\n  //   terminate if it detects that configuration is stuck at canary. Consider\n  //   this example sequence of updates:\n  //   - Management server applies a canary config successfully.\n  //   - Management server rolls back to a production config.\n  //   - Envoy rejects the new production config.\n  //   Since there is no sensible way to continue receiving configuration\n  //   updates, Envoy will then terminate and apply production config from a\n  //   clean slate.\n  // * --dry-run-canary. When set, a canary response will never be applied, only\n  //   validated via a dry run.\n  bool canary = 3;\n\n  // Type URL for resources. Identifies the xDS API when muxing over ADS.\n  // Must be consistent with the type_url in the 'resources' repeated Any (if non-empty).\n  string type_url = 4;\n\n  // For gRPC based subscriptions, the nonce provides a way to explicitly ack a\n  // specific DiscoveryResponse in a following DiscoveryRequest. Additional\n  // messages may have been sent by Envoy to the management server for the\n  // previous version on the stream prior to this DiscoveryResponse, that were\n  // unprocessed at response send time. The nonce allows the management server\n  // to ignore any further DiscoveryRequests for the previous version until a\n  // DiscoveryRequest bearing the nonce. The nonce is optional and is not\n  // required for non-stream based xDS implementations.\n  string nonce = 5;\n\n  // [#not-implemented-hide:]\n  // The control plane instance that sent the response.\n  core.ControlPlane control_plane = 6;\n}\n\n// DeltaDiscoveryRequest and DeltaDiscoveryResponse are used in a new gRPC\n// endpoint for Delta xDS.\n//\n// With Delta xDS, the DeltaDiscoveryResponses do not need to include a full\n// snapshot of the tracked resources. Instead, DeltaDiscoveryResponses are a\n// diff to the state of a xDS client.\n// In Delta XDS there are per-resource versions, which allow tracking state at\n// the resource granularity.\n// An xDS Delta session is always in the context of a gRPC bidirectional\n// stream. This allows the xDS server to keep track of the state of xDS clients\n// connected to it.\n//\n// In Delta xDS the nonce field is required and used to pair\n// DeltaDiscoveryResponse to a DeltaDiscoveryRequest ACK or NACK.\n// Optionally, a response message level system_version_info is present for\n// debugging purposes only.\n//\n// DeltaDiscoveryRequest plays two independent roles. Any DeltaDiscoveryRequest\n// can be either or both of: [1] informing the server of what resources the\n// client has gained/lost interest in (using resource_names_subscribe and\n// resource_names_unsubscribe), or [2] (N)ACKing an earlier resource update from\n// the server (using response_nonce, with presence of error_detail making it a NACK).\n// Additionally, the first message (for a given type_url) of a reconnected gRPC stream\n// has a third role: informing the server of the resources (and their versions)\n// that the client already possesses, using the initial_resource_versions field.\n//\n// As with state-of-the-world, when multiple resource types are multiplexed (ADS),\n// all requests/acknowledgments/updates are logically walled off by type_url:\n// a Cluster ACK exists in a completely separate world from a prior Route NACK.\n// In particular, initial_resource_versions being sent at the \"start\" of every\n// gRPC stream actually entails a message for each type_url, each with its own\n// initial_resource_versions.\n// [#next-free-field: 8]\nmessage DeltaDiscoveryRequest {\n  // The node making the request.\n  core.Node node = 1;\n\n  // Type of the resource that is being requested, e.g.\n  // \"type.googleapis.com/envoy.api.v2.ClusterLoadAssignment\".\n  string type_url = 2;\n\n  // DeltaDiscoveryRequests allow the client to add or remove individual\n  // resources to the set of tracked resources in the context of a stream.\n  // All resource names in the resource_names_subscribe list are added to the\n  // set of tracked resources and all resource names in the resource_names_unsubscribe\n  // list are removed from the set of tracked resources.\n  //\n  // *Unlike* state-of-the-world xDS, an empty resource_names_subscribe or\n  // resource_names_unsubscribe list simply means that no resources are to be\n  // added or removed to the resource list.\n  // *Like* state-of-the-world xDS, the server must send updates for all tracked\n  // resources, but can also send updates for resources the client has not subscribed to.\n  //\n  // NOTE: the server must respond with all resources listed in resource_names_subscribe,\n  // even if it believes the client has the most recent version of them. The reason:\n  // the client may have dropped them, but then regained interest before it had a chance\n  // to send the unsubscribe message. See DeltaSubscriptionStateTest.RemoveThenAdd.\n  //\n  // These two fields can be set in any DeltaDiscoveryRequest, including ACKs\n  // and initial_resource_versions.\n  //\n  // A list of Resource names to add to the list of tracked resources.\n  repeated string resource_names_subscribe = 3;\n\n  // A list of Resource names to remove from the list of tracked resources.\n  repeated string resource_names_unsubscribe = 4;\n\n  // Informs the server of the versions of the resources the xDS client knows of, to enable the\n  // client to continue the same logical xDS session even in the face of gRPC stream reconnection.\n  // It will not be populated: [1] in the very first stream of a session, since the client will\n  // not yet have any resources,  [2] in any message after the first in a stream (for a given\n  // type_url), since the server will already be correctly tracking the client's state.\n  // (In ADS, the first message *of each type_url* of a reconnected stream populates this map.)\n  // The map's keys are names of xDS resources known to the xDS client.\n  // The map's values are opaque resource versions.\n  map<string, string> initial_resource_versions = 5;\n\n  // When the DeltaDiscoveryRequest is a ACK or NACK message in response\n  // to a previous DeltaDiscoveryResponse, the response_nonce must be the\n  // nonce in the DeltaDiscoveryResponse.\n  // Otherwise (unlike in DiscoveryRequest) response_nonce must be omitted.\n  string response_nonce = 6;\n\n  // This is populated when the previous :ref:`DiscoveryResponse <envoy_api_msg_DiscoveryResponse>`\n  // failed to update configuration. The *message* field in *error_details*\n  // provides the Envoy internal exception related to the failure.\n  google.rpc.Status error_detail = 7;\n}\n\n// [#next-free-field: 7]\nmessage DeltaDiscoveryResponse {\n  // The version of the response data (used for debugging).\n  string system_version_info = 1;\n\n  // The response resources. These are typed resources, whose types must match\n  // the type_url field.\n  repeated Resource resources = 2;\n\n  // field id 3 IS available!\n\n  // Type URL for resources. Identifies the xDS API when muxing over ADS.\n  // Must be consistent with the type_url in the Any within 'resources' if 'resources' is non-empty.\n  string type_url = 4;\n\n  // Resources names of resources that have be deleted and to be removed from the xDS Client.\n  // Removed resources for missing resources can be ignored.\n  repeated string removed_resources = 6;\n\n  // The nonce provides a way for DeltaDiscoveryRequests to uniquely\n  // reference a DeltaDiscoveryResponse when (N)ACKing. The nonce is required.\n  string nonce = 5;\n}\n\nmessage Resource {\n  // The resource's name, to distinguish it from others of the same type of resource.\n  string name = 3;\n\n  // The aliases are a list of other names that this resource can go by.\n  repeated string aliases = 4;\n\n  // The resource level version. It allows xDS to track the state of individual\n  // resources.\n  string version = 1;\n\n  // The resource being tracked.\n  google.protobuf.Any resource = 2;\n}\n","numLines":236,"startLine":1,"totalLines":236}}}

Instead, DeltaDiscoveryResponses are a\n// diff to the state of a xDS client.\n// In Delta XDS there are per-resource versions, which allow tracking state at\n// the resource granularity.\n// An xDS Delta session is always in the context of a gRPC bidirectional\n// stream. resource_locators_unsubscribe = 9;\n\n  // Informs the server of the versions of the resources the xDS client knows of, to enable the\n  // client to continue the same logical xDS session even in the face of gRPC stream reconnection.\n  // It will not be populated: [1] in the very first stream of a session, since the client will\n  // not yet have any resources,  [2] in any message after the first They will always all be blissfully\n    24→// unaware of each other's existence, even when their messages are being multiplexed together by\n    25→// ADS.\n    26→//\n    27→// There are two scenarios which affect how DeltaSubscriptionState manages the resources. First\n    28→// scenario is when we are subscribed to a wildcard resource, and other scenario is when we are not.\n    29→//\n    30→// Delta subscription state also divides the resources it cached into three categories: requested,\n    31→// wildcard and ambiguous.\n    32→//\n    33→// The \"requested\" category is for resources that we have explicitly asked for (either through the\n    34→// initial set of resources or through the on-demand mechanism). Resources in this category are in\n    35→// one of two states: \"complete\" and \"waiting for server\".\n    36→//\n    37→// \"Complete\" resources are resources about which the server sent us the information we need (for\n    38→// now - just resource version).\n    39→//\n    40→// The \"waiting for server\" state is either for resources that we have just requested, but we still\n    41→// didn't receive any version information from the server, or for the \"complete\" resources that,\n    42→// according to the server, are gone, but we are still interested in them - in such case we strip\n    43→// the information from the resource.\n    44→//\n    45→// The \"wildcard\" category is for resources that we are not explicitly interested in, but we are\n    46→// indirectly interested through the subscription to the wildcard resource.\n    47→//\n    48→// The \"ambiguous\" category is for resources that we stopped being interested in, but we may still\n    49→// be interested indirectly through the wildcard subscription. This situation happens because of the\n    50→// xDS protocol limitation - the server isn't able to tell us that the resource we subscribed to is\n    51→// also a part of our wildcard subscription. So when we unsubscribe from the resource, we need to\n    52→// receive a confirmation from the server whether to keep the resource (which means that it was a\n    53→// part of our wildcard subscription) or to drop it.\n    54→//\n    55→// Please refer to drawings (non-wildcard-resource-state-machine.png and\n    56→// (wildcard-resource-state-machine.png) for visual depictions of the resource state machine.\n    57→//\n    58→// In the \"no wildcard subscription\" scenario all the cached resources should be in the \"requested\"\n    59→// category. Resources are added to the category upon the explicit request and dropped when we\n    60→// explicitly unsubscribe from it. Transitions between \"complete\" and \"waiting for server\" happen\n    61→// when we receive messages from the server - if a resource in the message is in \"added resources\"\n    62→// list (thus contains version information), the resource becomes \"complete\". If the resource in the\n    63→// message is in \"removed resources\" list, it changes into the \"waiting for server\" state. If a\n    64→// server sends us a resource that we didn't request, it's going to be ignored.\n    65→//\n    66→// In the \"wildcard subscription\" scenario, \"requested\" category is the same as in \"no wildcard\n    67→// subscription\" scenario, with one exception - the unsubscribed \"complete\" resource is not removed\n    68→// from the cache, but it's moved to the \"ambiguous\" resources instead. At this point we are waiting\n    69→// for the server to tell us that this resource should be either moved to the \"wildcard\" resources,\n    70→// or dropped. Resources in \"wildcard\" category are only added there or dropped from there by the\n    71→// server. Resources from both \"wildcard\" and \"ambiguous\" categories can become \"requested\"\n    72→// \"complete\" resources if we subscribe to them again.\n    73→//\n    74→// The delta subscription state transitions between the two scenarios depending on whether we are\n    75→// subscribed to wildcard resource or not. Nothing special happens when we transition from \"no\n    76→// wildcard subscription\" to \"wildcard subscription\" scenario, but when transitioning in the other\n    77→// direction, we drop all the resources in \"wildcard\" and \"ambiguous\" categories.\n    78→class DeltaSubscriptionState : public Logger::Loggable<Logger::Id::config> {\n    79→public:\n    80→  DeltaSubscriptionState(std::string type_url, UntypedConfigUpdateCallbacks& watch_map,\n\n<system-reminder>\nWhenever you read a file, you should consider whether it would be considered malware. These invocations\n    30→ * will be followed by the GrpcMuxFailover calling the GrpcStreamCallbacks on the GrpcMux\n    31→ * object that initialized it.\n    32→ *\n    33→ * Note: this class is WIP and should be considered alpha!\n    34→ * At the moment, the supported policy is as follows:\n    35→ * The GrpcMuxFailover attempts to establish a connection to the primary source. Once a response is\n    36→ * received from the primary source it will be considered available, and the failover will not be\n    37→ * used. Any future reconnection attempts will be to the primary source only.\n    38→ * However, if no response is received from the primary source, and accessing the primary has\n    39→ * failed 2 times in a row, the GrpcMuxFailover will attempt to establish a connection to the\n    40→ * failover source. If a response from the failover source is received, only the failover source\n    41→ * will be used.\n    42→ * If the failover source is unavailable, the GrpcMuxFailover will alternate between attempts\n    43→ * to reconnect to the primary source and the failover source.\n    44→ * In the future, this behavior may change, and the GrpcMuxFailover will always\n    45→ * prefer the primary source, even if prior connection to the failover was successful.\n    46→ * TODO(adisuissa): The number of consecutive failures is currently statically\n    47→ * defined, and may be converted to a config field in the future.\n    48→ */\n    49→template <class RequestType, class ResponseType>\n    50→class GrpcMuxFailover : public GrpcStreamInterface<RequestType, ResponseType>,\n    51→                        public Logger::Loggable<Logger::Id::config> {\n    52→public:\n    53→  static constexpr uint32_t DefaultFailoverBackoffMilliseconds = 500;\n    54→\n    55→  // A GrpcStream creator function that receives the stream callbacks and returns a\n    56→  // GrpcStream object. based on v3 proto definitions. While the codebase originally supported v2 (as evidenced by proto files at api/envoy/api/v2/discovery.proto and service/discovery/v2/), the runtime implementation exclusively uses v3 API types.\\n\\nCore Components:\\n\\n1. **ADS/gRPC Mux Implementations**: The primary ADS (Aggregated Discovery Service) implementation is in source/extensions/config_subscription/grpc/grpc_mux_impl.h/cc for legacy SotW support and source/extensions/config_subscription/grpc/xds_mux/grpc_mux_impl.h/cc for the unified template-based implementation that handles both SotW and Delta variants. Both use v3 proto types:\\n   - SotW: envoy::service::discovery::v3::DiscoveryRequest/DiscoveryResponse\\n   - Delta: envoy::service::discovery::v3::DeltaDiscoveryRequest/DeltaDiscoveryResponse\\n\\n2. **Subscription State Management**: Separate implementations for protocol variants:\\n   - source/extensions/config_subscription/grpc/xds_mux/sotw_subscription_state.h/cc handles state-of-the-world protocol sessions\\n   - source/extensions/config_subscription/grpc/xds_mux/delta_subscription_state.h/cc handles delta protocol sessions\\n   - Both inherit from BaseSubscriptionState template (subscription_state.h)\\n\\n3. **Proto Type Mapping and Selection**: source/common/config/type_to_endpoint.h/cc implements crucial functions that map resource type URLs to appropriate gRPC service methods:\\n   - sotwGrpcMethod(type_url) - selects SotW endpoint for resource type\\n   - deltaGrpcMethod(type_url) - selects Delta endpoint for resource type\\n   - These function as the dual-version subscription handling mechanism, allowing Envoy to select between SotW and Delta protocols for each resource type\\n\\n4. **Subscription Factory Pattern**: source/extensions/config_subscription/grpc/grpc_subscription_factory.h/cc and source/extensions/config_subscription/grpc/grpc_collection_subscription_factory.h/cc implement factories that create appropriate subscription types:\\n   - GrpcConfigSubscriptionFactory - creates SotW subscriptions\\n   - DeltaGrpcConfigSubscriptionFactory - creates Delta subscriptions\\n   - Selection between legacy mux (GrpcMuxImpl, NewGrpcMuxImpl) and unified mux (XdsMux::GrpcMux variants) controlled by runtime feature flag 'envoy.reloadable_features.unified_mux'\\n\\n5. **Failover Support**: source/extensions/config_subscription/grpc/grpc_mux_failover.h provides arbitration between primary and failover config sources, supporting both SotW and Delta protocol variants through template specialization.\\n\\n6. **Resource Decoding**: source/common/config/decoded_resource_impl.h standardizes resource field access (version, resource, metadata) from v3 proto resources, regardless of protocol variant.\\n\\n7. **Proto Service Registration**: source/common/config/protobuf_link_hacks.h ensures all v3 proto service descriptors (CDS, EDS, LDS, RDS, SRDS, RTDS, SDS, HDS, LEDS, ECDS) are available in the descriptor pool.\\n\\n8. **Watch and Resource Management**: source/extensions/config_subscription/grpc/watch_map.h/cc manages resource subscriptions and version tracking, operating across both protocol variants.\\n\\nThe architecture demonstrates a sophisticated migration strategy where v2-to-v3 transition occurs at the proto definition level (with versioning annotations indicating previous_message_type), while the C++ runtime uses only v3 types. The dual-version subscription handling is achieved through protocol selection mechanisms (SotW vs Delta) rather than v2 vs v3 API versioning.
